<li id="cite_note-Stepanov-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Stepanov_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Stepanov_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFLo_Russo,_Graziano_(1997)" class="citation web cs1">Lo Russo, Graziano (1997). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.stlport.org/resources/StepanovUSA.html">"An Interview with A. Stepanov (Edizioni Infomedia srl.)"</a>. STLport.org<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">21 December</span> 2017</span>. <q><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Stepanov" title="Alexander Stepanov">Alexander Stepanov</a>: "...I also discovered books of two great computer scientists from whose work I learned the scientific foundation of my trade: <a href="/wiki/Donald_Knuth" title="Donald Knuth">Donald Knuth</a> and Edsger Dijkstra. Knuth taught me the answers. Dijkstra taught me the questions. Time and time again I come back to their works for new insights."</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=An+Interview+with+A.+Stepanov+%28Edizioni+Infomedia+srl.%29&amp;rft.pub=STLport.org&amp;rft.au=Lo+Russo%2C+Graziano+%281997%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.stlport.org%2Fresources%2FStepanovUSA.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.britannica.com/biography/Edsger-Dijkstra">https://www.britannica.com/biography/Edsger-Dijkstra</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFIstrail2008">Istrail (2008)</a>. "A prolific writer, he [Dijkstra] authored more than 1,300 papers, many written by hand in his precise and elegant script. They were essays and parables; fairy tales and warnings; comprehensive explanation and pedagogical pretext. Most were about mathematics and computer science; others were trip reports that are more revealing about their author than about the people and places visited. This “Dijkstranian style” of writing flourished on the frontier between technical computing science and the philosophy substantiating its distinguished development. It was his habit to copy each paper and circulate it to a small group of colleagues who would copy and forward the papers to another limited group of scientists. (...) I read them with joy and excitement and my love for mathematics and computer science has been influenced in no small measure by his works."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFGries1978" class="citation book cs1"><a href="/wiki/David_Gries" title="David Gries">Gries, David</a> (1978). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=JdziBwAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA7"><i>Programming Methodology: A Collection of Articles by Members of IFIP WG2.3</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-DijkstraNYT-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-DijkstraNYT_18-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DijkstraNYT_18-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFMarkoff2002" class="citation news cs1">Markoff, John (10 August 2002). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2002/08/10/obituaries/10DIJK.html">"Edsger Dijkstra: Physicist Who Shaped Computer Era"</a>. <i>New York Times</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFKnuth1974" class="citation journal cs1"><a href="/wiki/Donald_Knuth" title="Donald Knuth">Knuth, Donald</a> (1974). "Structured Programming with Go To Statements". <i>Computing Surveys</i>. <b>6</b> (4): 261–301. <a href="/wiki/CiteSeerX_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="CiteSeerX (identifier)">CiteSeerX</a>&#160;<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/summary?doi=10.1.1.103.6084">10.1.1.103.6084</a></span>. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1145%2F356635.356640">10.1145/356635.356640</a>. <a href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:207630080">207630080</a>. <q>A revolution is taking place in the way we write programs and teach programming, because we are beginning to understand the associated mental processes more deeply. It is impossible to read the recent book <i>Structured Programming</i> [by Dijkstra, <a href="/wiki/Ole-Johan_Dahl" title="Ole-Johan Dahl">Ole-Johan Dahl</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hoare" title="Tony Hoare">Tony Hoare</a> (1972)], without having it change your life. The reason for this revolution and its future prospects have been aptly described by E.W. Dijkstra in his 1972 Turing Award Lecture, <i>The Humble Programmer</i>.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Computing+Surveys&amp;rft.atitle=Structured+Programming+with+Go+To+Statements&amp;rft.volume=6&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=261-301&amp;rft.date=1974&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fciteseerx.ist.psu.edu%2Fviewdoc%2Fsummary%3Fdoi%3D10.1.1.103.6084%23id-name%3DCiteSeerX&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A207630080%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1145%2F356635.356640&amp;rft.aulast=Knuth&amp;rft.aufirst=Donald&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Meyer2009p188-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Meyer2009p188_25-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Meyer2009p188_25-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Meyer2009p188_25-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFMeyer2009" class="citation book cs1"><a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Meyer" title="Bertrand Meyer">Meyer, Bertrand</a> (2009). <i>Touch of Class: Learning to Program Well with Objects and Contracts</i>. Springer. p.&#160;188. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3540921448" title="Special:BookSources/978-3540921448"><bdi>978-3540921448</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Touch+of+Class%3A+Learning+to+Program+Well+with+Objects+and+Contracts&amp;rft.pages=188&amp;rft.pub=Springer&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.isbn=978-3540921448&amp;rft.aulast=Meyer&amp;rft.aufirst=Bertrand&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFLamport2015">Lamport (2015)</a>. "While <a href="/wiki/Concurrent_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Concurrent program">concurrent program</a> execution had been considered for years, the computer science of concurrency began with Edsger Dijkstra's seminal 1965 paper that introduced the mutual exclusion problem. (...) The first scientific examination of <a href="/wiki/Fault_tolerance" title="Fault tolerance">fault tolerance</a> was Dijkstra's seminal 1974 paper on self-stabilization. (...) The ensuing decades have seen a huge growth of interest in concurrency—particularly in distributed systems. Looking back at the origins of the field, what stands out is the fundamental role played by Edsger Dijkstra, to whom this history is dedicated."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-DijkstraPrize-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-DijkstraPrize_27-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DijkstraPrize_27-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DijkstraPrize_27-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.podc.org/dijkstra">"Edsger W. Dijkstra Prize in Distributed Computing"</a>. ACM Symposium on Principles of Distributed Computing.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Edsger+W.+Dijkstra+Prize+in+Distributed+Computing&amp;rft.pub=ACM+Symposium+on+Principles+of+Distributed+Computing&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.podc.org%2Fdijkstra&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span><br />–
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eatcs.org/index.php/dijkstra-prize">"Dijkstra Prize"</a>. European Association for Theoretical Computer Science (EATCS).</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Dijkstra+Prize&amp;rft.pub=European+Association+for+Theoretical+Computer+Science+%28EATCS%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.eatcs.org%2Findex.php%2Fdijkstra-prize&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span><br />–
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.disc-conference.org/wp/dijkstra-prize/">"Dijkstra Prize"</a>. International Symposium on Distributed Computing (DISC).</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Dijkstra+Prize&amp;rft.pub=International+Symposium+on+Distributed+Computing+%28DISC%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.disc-conference.org%2Fwp%2Fdijkstra-prize%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span><br />–
"The <a href="/wiki/Edsger_W._Dijkstra_Prize_in_Distributed_Computing" class="mw-redirect" title="Edsger W. Dijkstra Prize in Distributed Computing">Edsger W. Dijkstra Prize in Distributed Computing</a> is named for Edsger Wybe Dijkstra (1930–2002), a pioneer in the area of distributed computing. His foundational work on concurrency primitives (such as the semaphore), concurrency problems (such as mutual exclusion and deadlock), reasoning about concurrent systems, and self-stabilization comprises one of the most important supports upon which the field of distributed computing is built. No other individual has had a larger influence on research in principles of distributed computing."</span>
</li>

New York, NY, USA: Springer-Verlag. pp.&#160;60–66. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-387-90652-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-387-90652-2"><bdi>978-0-387-90652-2</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=On+the+role+of+scientific+thought&amp;rft.btitle=Selected+writings+on+Computing%3A+A+Personal+Perspective&amp;rft.place=New+York%2C+NY%2C+USA&amp;rft.pages=60-66&amp;rft.pub=Springer-Verlag&amp;rft.date=1982&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-387-90652-2&amp;rft.aulast=Dijkstra&amp;rft.aufirst=Edsger+W&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.cs.utexas.edu%2Fusers%2FEWD%2Ftranscriptions%2FEWD04xx%2FEWD447.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFBrownCraigHesterAmsden2003" class="citation book cs1">Brown, Kyle; Craig, Gary; Hester, Greg; Amsden, Jim; Pitt, David; Jakab, Peter M.; Berg, Daniel; Stinehour, Russell; Weitzel, Mark (2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=KBlXQPNGOmIC"><i>Enterprise Java Programming with IBM WebSphere</i></a> (2nd&#160;ed.). IBM Press. p.&#160;5. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-321-18579-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-321-18579-2"><bdi>978-0-321-18579-2</bdi></a>. <q>Most experienced IT professionals will agree that developing and adhering to a standard architecture is key to the success of large-scale software development. Computer pioneer Edsger Dijkstra validated this notion when he developed THE operating system in 1968. Since then, layered architectures have proved their viability in technological domains, such as hardware and networking. Layering has proved itself in the operating system domain; however, the same benefits are available when applied to e-commerce or to thin client–oriented applications. Layered architectures have become essential in supporting the iterative development process by promoting reusability, scalability, and maintainability.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Enterprise+Java+Programming+with+IBM+WebSphere&amp;rft.pages=5&amp;rft.edition=2nd&amp;rft.pub=IBM+Press&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-321-18579-2&amp;rft.aulast=Brown&amp;rft.aufirst=Kyle&amp;rft.au=Craig%2C+Gary&amp;rft.au=Hester%2C+Greg&amp;rft.au=Amsden%2C+Jim&amp;rft.au=Pitt%2C+David&amp;rft.au=Jakab%2C+Peter+M.&amp;rft.au=Berg%2C+Daniel&amp;rft.au=Stinehour%2C+Russell&amp;rft.au=Weitzel%2C+Mark&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DKBlXQPNGOmIC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEdsger+W.+Dijkstra" class="Z3988"></span></span>
